I'm not particularly into the whole organic movement, but it did concern me a bit that I still don't know what some of the listed ingredients actually are...but as I am certainly no expert on holistics or organics, they may very well be something truly organic. I don't know. Pros: 1. NO ITCH so far! I have been itch-free since I began using this shampoo. 2. My hair actually feels clean...it does what shampoo is supposed to actually do! 3. It lathers pretty good. I realize without sulfates, there won't be much lather (I have experienced this with Burt's Bees), but I have had no trouble getting this shampoo to lather. 4. Still within the affordable range. Some organic stuff can be outrageously expensive. This is still more than I would like to spend on a shampoo, but trust me, it's worth it to stop that itch. Cons: 1. Smells somewhat like cardboard to me. Not a bad smell...just...boring and kind of ugh. 2. Dries my hair a bit. But I used the silk conditioner by the same company and that seems to solve this problem. The conditioner also smells something like warm vanilla sugar, so once I use that I forget all about the cardboard shampoo smell. If any of this changes, I will update the review to reflect it, but for now, all is well and I really am overall quite happy with it.

Regular shampoos also lather right away, so you don't REALLY need to wash your hair twice (ya know, the wash, rinse, repeat thing). With this shampoo, I did not get much lather the first time I washed my hair, so I felt like I needed to repeat. During the repeat wash, I got a really good lather and was really pleased! This means I'll be paying up to twice as much for less product and be using twice as much product each time I wash my hair.<br /><br />However, my above comparison was to non-natural shampoos. Let's try another natural shampoo I used. I think it's just called 100% Pure because that's all it really says on the bottle lol. It was the cheapest one I could find before I found this one. It's all natural and organic. There was barely any lather at all even on the repeat wash, and I felt like I had to use much more than the Maple Holistics shampoo just to cover my whole head. It also made my scalp dry and flaky which never happens and certainly did NOT happen with the argan oil shampoo. The 100% Pure shampoo was $25 for a 13oz bottle, and like I said, I had to use much more than the Maple Holistics shampoo, so it was more money for less product (well, I only bought an 8oz bottle here on Amazon, but 100% Pure is still more expensive) and I had to use about twice as much shampoo per shot than the argan oil stuff. Actually I think it was more. I had to use about two quarter sizes of the argan oil shampoo (one for the first wash and slightly more for the repeat) and for the 100% Pure stuff I used an amount a bit bigger than a silver dollar on the first wash and again on the repeat wash before I was satisfied. So that's 50 cents versus two dollars :P<br /><br />The one thing I liked more about the 100% Pure shampoo was that on the ingredient list it had a laymen's description in parentheses next to any ingredient that sounded complicated or foreign. So for example, next to &#34;Fucus Vesiculosus&#34; it had &#34;(Kelp)&#34; and next to &#34;Tocopherol&#34; it had &#34;(Vitamin E)&#34;. Maple Holistics does this with the last several ingredients, but mostly the ingredients list on this Maple Holistics shampoo is difficult to read and requires research if you want to really want to know it's natural and understand what's in it. I would love a bit more info on the ingredients in Maple Holistics products. So far I'm really just taking people's word for it that it's 100% natural and am still researching the ingredients a bit myself.<br />For example, when I saw an ingredient like Sodium Lauryl Glucose Carboxylate, I thought to myself &#34;Heeeyyy....that doesn't look like it would be a natural ingredient!&#34;, so I looked it up and after some reading found the simplest explanation on truthinaging.com:<br />&#34;...according to TriNature.com, it is a foaming agent that is derived from glucoside from coconut and corn. It is also used as a natural replacement for the ingredient known as sodium laureth sulfate, or SLES.&#34; So it comes from coconut and corn.<br />I also looked up Sodium Lauroamphoacetate and according to naturopathica.com: &#34;Sodium Lauroamphoacetate is a gentle, amphoteric foaming and cleansing agent derived from natural and renewable resources. Based on coconut oil, this mild ingredient creates excellent foam structure and feel. It is bio-degradable and well tolerated by all skin types.&#34;<br /><br />I haven't finished looking up all the other ingredients. It would just be nice for there to be a simpler ingredients listed instead of the first two-thirds of the list looking like gibberish lol or for the bottle to come with a small info sheet on ALL the ingredients that you see in the list. Maple Holistics DOES try to cover the ingredients in the bottle on an information card I received with the shampoo, it just doesn't go over the first two thirds of the list where the most complicated looking ingredients are that people would probably be most likely to suspect were made in a lab or something. ***The other option would be to do what naturopathica did and just put a list of product ingredients with their descriptions on the website instead of wasting paper on an info card or info sheet to send with the shampoo. Naturopathica put all of the ingredients in all of their products in an &#34;ingredient glossary&#34;.*** The 100% Pure shampoo I used had a relatively small and simple ingredient list, but the Maple Holistics shampoo does work much better, so my opinion is that the quality outweighs this con.<br /><br />So compared to non-natural shampoos, this shampoo is more expensive and may not be for people on a tight budget, but it gets my hair as clean, leaves my hair looking shinier, leaves my scalp feeling much better, and is healthier for my hair and scalp. Compared to other natural shampoos I've seen and the one I bought, the price is definitely better. Compared to the only other natural shampoo I tried (and many others according to other people), it lathers much better and I can use much less.
